### The Legacy Vault Print and Legacy Portrait

**Origin of these products:**

These products emerged from a real experience. A Sunnycrest owner created an informal print of a vault top Legacy design for a grieving family. The grandmother received it, cried, and it has hung on her living room wall ever since — years later. This is the most powerful product validation possible: a real family, a real emotional response, a product permanently displayed in a home. The question is not whether families want this. The question is how to make it as beautiful as the moment deserves.

---

#### The Legacy Vault Print

The exact reproduction of the vault top Legacy design — printed as a large format piece for the family's home.

```
What makes this uniquely powerful:

  The vault design was chosen by the family
  to represent their loved one
  It goes into the ground with them
  The print stays with the living
  
  One design — two destinations:
    One goes with them
    One stays with you
    
  The family holds the print
    and knows that the same image
    is on their loved one's vault
    in the ground
    
  That connection — between the living
    and the buried — through a shared
    object — is something no other
    memorial product has ever offered
    
  It is not a representation of them
  It is literally the same thing
    that is with them
    
  That is a different category
    of emotional significance entirely
```

**The arrangement conference moment:**

```
Family finishes designing the vault Legacy →
Director says:
  "This is beautiful.
   This is what will be on his vault.
   
   A lot of families want to keep
   this exact design at home —
   the same piece that's with him.
   
   We can print this for you
   on archival paper, canvas, or metal.
   
   Would you like one for the family?"
   
No selling required
They just designed it
They love it
They want it
```

**Formats and materials:**

```
Fine art archival paper — frameable
Canvas wrap — ready to hang
Metal print — modern, luminous
Wood print — warm, craftsman-appropriate

Sizes:
  16×20 standard
  24×30 premium
  Custom dimensions

Multiple copies:
  Family home
  Each adult child
  Grandchildren (smaller format)
  Average family order: 3-5 prints
```

**The manufacturer connection:**

```
The manufacturer already has
  the design file —
  they produced the vault
  
  Options:
    Manufacturer fulfills print orders
      as additional revenue stream
    Dedicated print vendor
      cross-tenant receives design file
      
  Either way:
    Design file lives in vault
    Order flows cross-tenant automatically
    Family receives the same thing
      that's with their loved one
```

---

A companion product — an AI-designed tribute piece capturing the person's life story in a professionally designed large format print. Different from the vault print — this is the narrative, not the emblem.

```
Design elements:
  The tribute text — AI-crafted from Scribe:
    Not a list of facts
    A narrative portrait in beautiful language
    
  Photography:
    Best photo from vault
    Professionally processed
    Portrait quality
    
  Design language from Story Thread:
    Military → clean, dignified, structured
    Craftsman → warm wood tones, textured
    Gardener → organic, floral elements
    Catholic → appropriate religious artistry
    
  The QR code (discreet):
    "To hear [Name]'s story"
    Scan → family vault portal
    Physical piece connects to
      permanent digital memorial
```

**These two products displayed together:**

```
"This is what marked his place.
 This is who he was."

The vault design: visual and symbolic
The portrait: narrative and textual

Different products
Complementary meaning
Many families want both
Displayed together they tell
  the complete story
```

**Revenue:**

```
Legacy Vault Print:
  Average 3 prints per family: $450
  150 cases/year: $67,500
  Portal/website reorders: $36,000/year
  Total estimate: ~$103,500/year

Legacy Portrait:
  Average 2 prints per family: $300
  150 cases/year: $45,000
  Portal/website reorders: $20,000/year
  Total estimate: ~$65,000/year

Combined: ~$168,500/year
From products that currently don't exist
Triggered by a design already made

## 6.11 Wilbert Strategic Partnership — The Casket and Monument Breakthrough

**The strategic alignment:**

Cremation is an existential threat to Wilbert's burial vault business. Their response — expanding into caskets, monuments, and embalming chemicals through the same licensee distribution network — is the right strategy. The execution challenge is distribution: getting Wilbert products in front of families at the moment of decision, in an experience compelling enough to displace incumbent relationships with Batesville and existing monument companies.

Bridgeable solves this permanently.

**What Wilbert needs:**

```
Casket market share growth:
  Funeral homes default to Batesville
  because Batesville has showrooms
  and dedicated sales reps
  Wilbert has neither at the funeral home level
  The licensee is a concrete company
    not a dedicated casket sales organization
  
Monument market share growth:
  Families go to separate monument companies
  after the arrangement conference
  Licensee has no presence at that decision point
  Revenue leaks out of the Wilbert network
  
Embalming chemical recurring revenue:
  Reorder process is manual and friction-filled
  Funeral homes often switch on price
    because there's no loyalty mechanism
```

**What Bridgeable delivers:**

```
For caskets:
  Every Bridgeable arrangement conference
    = full Wilbert casket catalog presented
    = photorealistic 3D experience
    = AI personalization to the deceased
    = no Batesville showroom in the room
    = order generated automatically
    = no sales rep ever needed
    
For monuments:
  Monument Composer captures the sale
    at the arrangement conference —
    before the family leaves
    before they call another monument company
    with the cemetery specification compliance
    that eliminates post-sale problems
    
For embalming chemicals:
  Automatic reordering from vault inventory →
  Funeral home never runs out →
  Never has a reason to evaluate competitors →
  Recurring revenue becomes permanent
  
For stationery (new product line):
  Stationery Composer creates a new
    Wilbert revenue stream
    that doesn't currently exist →
  Bridgeable provides the platform
    and Wilbert provides the brand
    and distribution network
```

**The exclusivity model:**

Initial Bridgeable adoption with Wilbert products only on the platform creates structural market share growth:

```
Funeral home adopts Bridgeable →
Personalization Studio only shows
  Wilbert caskets and monuments →
Every arrangement conference
  = Wilbert product presentation →
Director never walks to the
  Batesville showroom anymore →
Wilbert captures every Bridgeable adoption
  as guaranteed market share →
No sales rep required →
No showroom investment required →
Growth scales with Bridgeable adoption
```

**The new CEO conversation — what to say:**

The one-sentence version if the topic arises at any Wilbert interaction:

*"I can put Wilbert's caskets and monuments in front of every family at every arrangement conference on the platform, in an experience so meaningful that directors will never go back to a showroom — and the order flows automatically without a sales rep."*

The full pitch when the private meeting happens:

*"Cremation is shrinking the vault market. You've responded by expanding into caskets, monuments, and memorial products. The strategy is right. The execution challenge is distribution — getting your products in front of families at the moment of decision. Bridgeable solves that permanently. Every arrangement conference on the platform is a Personalization Studio session. Every session presents Wilbert caskets, monuments, and now stationery, in an experience so compelling that families design their loved one's complete memorial in one sitting. The orders flow automatically. No sales reps. No showrooms. No friction. I provide the platform and the experience. You provide the products. We split the growth."*

**The Wilbert ERP integration:**

Wilbert is building an ERP for licensee ordering of Wilbert products. This is not a competing system — it solves Wilbert's problem (ordering visibility) while Bridgeable solves the licensee's problem (running their entire business). The integration model:

```
Order placed in Bridgeable →
Automatically submitted to Wilbert ERP
  in their required format →
Confirmation and tracking flows back
  to Bridgeable vault →
Licensee never touches Wilbert ERP directly →
Wilbert gets the data they need →
Licensee gets seamless experience →

Bridgeable becomes the front end
  for the Wilbert ordering relationship
  while being the full platform
  for everything else
  
This positions Bridgeable as indispensable
  even within the Wilbert ERP ecosystem
```

**How Wilbert products flow through the licensee network — critical architecture note:**

All Wilbert product lines flow through the same licensee distribution model. Wilbert sells wholesale to licensees. Licensees sell to funeral homes and cemeteries. This is identical to how burial vaults work — and burial vault ordering is already built.

This means:

```
CRITICAL: No catalog API access needed from Wilbert corporate
  
Licensees already have:
  Full casket catalog — same as vault catalog
  Casket pricing — wholesale, same model as vaults
  Monument catalog — through Memorial Monuments
  Embalming chemical catalog and pricing
  Complete ordering relationship already established
  
The Casket Composer, Monument Composer,
  and Chemical reordering are ALL UNBLOCKED
  
No waiting for Wilbert cooperation
No catalog negotiation
No API access request
No external dependency
  
The build is entirely within your control
```

**The four Wilbert product lines on Bridgeable — revised:**

  Already built ✓

  Casket Composer: build now — UNBLOCKED ✓

**Professional development — CE Accreditation Program:**

```
"Wilbert Certified Funeral Professional" — NFDA accredited

Course catalog (all CE eligible):
  "The Modern Arrangement Conference"       3 credits
  "Pre-Planning: Converting Conversations"  2 credits

  "FTC Compliance and Transparency"         2 credits
  "Veterans and Military Funeral Services"  2 credits
  "Cultural Competency in Death Care"       2 credits
  "Monument and Memorial Selection"         1 credit
  "Digital Memorial Experiences"            1 credit

Revenue: ~$600/director/year. 20% of 35,000 directors = $4.2M annual.
Organic adoption engine: directors come for CE credits, stay for the platform.
Skills Passport credential — portable, visible to hiring funeral homes.
Accreditation timeline: Apply to NFDA now, 3-6 month approval, launch at September.
Handled by Bridgeable Legal — credentialing application process.
```

### Licensee Territory Rights — The Structural Protection

Licensees are historically paranoid about Wilbert projects going around them to funeral home customers. The solution is architecture, not messaging. Licensee revenue must be built into every transaction structurally.

**Revenue split per product:**
```
Memorial Stationery ($350):    Wilbert 17% / Licensee 14% / Bridgeable 69%
Digital Memorial ($300):       Wilbert 10% / Licensee 15% / Bridgeable 75%
Memorial Jewelry ($500):       Wilbert 10% / Licensee 15% / Bridgeable 75%
CE Credits ($600/yr):          Wilbert 10% / Licensee 15% / Bridgeable 75%
Aftercare ($1,200/yr):         Wilbert 10% / Licensee 15% / Bridgeable 75%
Website Builder ($150/mo):     Wilbert 10% / Licensee 15% / Bridgeable 75%
```

**Annual passive territory revenue — 50 FH territory:**
```
Stationery (3,000 cases × $50):           $150,000
Digital memorial (3,000 × $45):           $135,000
CE credits (60 directors × $90):            $5,400
Aftercare (25 FH × $180):                  $4,500
Website builder (35 FH × $22 × 12):        $9,240
Memorial jewelry (500 families × $75):      $7,500
Total passive annual territory revenue:  ~$312,000
```
For doing nothing except being on the platform and maintaining existing FH relationships. Growing with every new product launched.

### The Territory Addendum — Piggybacking on the Wilbert Agreement

Wilbert already has an executed license agreement with all 250 licensees. Territory definitions are established, understood, and trusted. A one-page addendum extends those rights to digital products — inheriting decades of trust without requiring a new legal relationship.

```
BRIDGEABLE DIGITAL PRODUCTS TERRITORY RIGHTS ADDENDUM
(Addendum to Wilbert License Agreement)

1. Territory Definition — identical to existing Wilbert vault territory
2. Territory Revenue — per Schedule A, paid monthly via Bridgeable Pay
3. Automatic Application — covers all current AND future Bridgeable products
   New products added to Schedule A with 30 days notice. No new agreement needed.
4. Territorial Exclusivity — same protection as existing vault territory
5. Structural Protection — rates cannot be reduced without licensee consent
   No product launches without territory rate established first
6. Continuation — survives duration of Wilbert License Agreement

SCHEDULE A (living document):
  Memorial Stationery: 14% | Digital Memorial: 15% | Jewelry: 15%
  CE Credits: 15% | Aftercare: 15% | Website: 15% | Pre-Planning: 12%
  [Future products: rate announced 30 days before launch, auto-included]
```

**Why Wilbert Legal approves this:** It solves their licensee cooperation problem permanently. A network earning $300k/year from territory rights is the most cooperative network Wilbert has ever had.

**The September execution:**
```
Before September:
  Bridgeable Legal drafts addendum — 30 days
  Wilbert Legal reviews — 60 day buffer
  Final version ready, printed copies at meeting

After the demo at September:
  "This is a one-page addendum to your existing Wilbert agreement.
   Same territory you already have, covering every Bridgeable product.
   Over $300,000 a year in passive revenue for a 50-FH territory.
   Every new product I build automatically adds to it.
   Wilbert's legal team has reviewed it.
   We have pens."
```

**Opening the September meeting — address the history directly:**
```
"I know the history. I know what some Wilbert projects
 felt like from the licensee side. I'm a licensee. I felt it too.

 So before I show you anything — here's how the money works.
 Every digital product Bridgeable sells in your territory,
 you get a cut. Automatically. Built into the economics.
 Not a promise. Architecture.

 This platform exists for you. Not for Wilbert.
 Not for the funeral homes. For you.

 Now let me show you what it looks like."

Then demo the family experience.
The room is already yours before you show a single screen.
```

**Bridgeable Legal priority list:**
```
IMMEDIATE (file before any public demo):
  Patents: color dot system, camera logic, production planner,
  Personalization Studio. Public demo = public disclosure = invalidation.

30 DAYS: Territory addendum drafted, sent to Wilbert Legal
60 DAYS: Addendum final + NFDA CE application filed

BACKGROUND: MEWA formation, ILC charter prep, state CE approvals

### The Data Intelligence Offer — What Bridgeable Gives Wilbert for Free

**What Wilbert's platform captures:**

```
Website analytics:
  Page views, click rates, time on site
  
Ad conversion tracking:
  Clicks to visits to information requests
  
Basic ordering metrics:
  Orders placed, products ordered,
  order value over time
  
This is standard digital marketing data
Google Analytics provides most of it free
It tells Wilbert:
  "People found our website
   and some of them ordered products"
   
That is the beginning of the story
Not the story itself
```

**What Bridgeable captures:**

```
Top of funnel (what Wilbert measures):
  Website visits ✓
  Ad conversions ✓
  Information requests ✓

Middle of funnel (what Wilbert misses):
  Which funeral homes use which licensees
  How many arrangement conferences
    per funeral home per month
  Which products get presented
    in which conferences
  How far into the Studio families get
  Which personalization options selected
  Which AI suggestions accepted vs. overridden
  How long families spend on each Composer

Bottom of funnel (never seen before):
  What gets ordered and why —
    connected to the specific arrangement
    conference that generated it
  Which director presentations convert
    at highest rates
  Which personalization combinations
    generate highest order values
  Which territories are underpenetrated
    relative to death rate data

Post-funnel (doesn't exist anywhere):
  Family portal engagement after service
  Pre-need conversion rates cross-tenant
  Monument and stationery attachment rates
  Referral attribution — which family
    experiences generate new FH customers
  Anniversary and follow-up conversion
```

**The arrangement conference is a black box to every other platform:**

```
Every ordering portal, every ERP,
  every analytics platform
  sees what happens before
  and after the arrangement conference
  
None of them have ever been
  inside the room
  
Bridgeable is inside that room
  for every case on the platform
  
That data has never existed
No competitor has it
No competitor can get it
  without being Bridgeable
  
This is the permanent data moat
```

**The specific data products Wilbert receives:**

```
1. Network Health Dashboard (real-time):
   Active arrangement conferences today
   Wilbert product attachment rates by territory
   Licensee performance rankings
   Funeral home adoption by market
   Geographic coverage gaps vs. death rate data

2. Product Intelligence Report (monthly):
   Which Wilbert products convert best
   Which personalization options drive
     highest order values
   Which products are losing to competitors
   New product signals — what families
     request that doesn't exist yet

3. Licensee Performance Analytics:
   Funeral home adoption rate per licensee
   Arrangement conference volume
   Wilbert attachment rate
   Territory revenue generated
   Competitive product leakage
   Specific training recommendations

4. Market Opportunity Map:
   Death rates by region
   Current Wilbert market penetration
   Gaps between death rate and order volume
   Competitor activity indicators
   Underpenetrated territories

5. Arrangement Conference Intelligence:
   Average time in each Composer
   Personalization option popularity
   Price sensitivity by market
   Family decision patterns
   Director presentation effectiveness

6. Predictive Analytics:
   Which funeral homes at risk of switching
   Which territories need attention
   Which product categories will grow/shrink
   Seasonal demand forecasting
```

**The CEO conversation:**

```
"You talked about conversion rates
 on ad spend and website analytics today.
 
 That data tells you how many people

 generates — because I think it's
 what you actually need to grow

 by territory.

 which funeral directors are actually
 selling your products well

 than the ones who aren't.
 
 Website analytics shows you
 the top of the funnel.

 inside the arrangement conference —
 the moment the sale is actually made.
 
 That data has never existed.
 
 You get it for free
 as a byproduct of endorsing
 a platform your licensees
 already want to use."

### Open Platform Strategy — Bridgeable Serves the Licensee's Entire Business

**The political reality:**

Some Wilbert licensees sell competing vault products — Triguard and others — in addition to Wilbert products. At the ESP announcement meeting, Wilbert told these licensees their platform would not support competing products. The response was essentially "tough luck."

This created resentment among mixed-product licensees and an adoption ceiling for Wilbert's platform. It also created an opportunity for Bridgeable.

**Bridgeable's position:**

```
Bridgeable is a licensee platform
  not a Wilbert platform
  
A licensee platform serves the
  licensee's entire business —
  not just the part that benefits Wilbert
  
If a licensee sells Triguard:
  Bridgeable handles Triguard orders
  
If a licensee sells competing caskets:
  Bridgeable handles those too
  
If a licensee sells any product
  from any supplier:
  Bridgeable manages all of it
  
This is the "licensee first" principle
  made concrete in the most
  politically charged way possible
```

**Why this doesn't hurt Wilbert — it helps them:**

```
The "wins on merit" argument:

Wilbert products in Bridgeable:
  Full Personalization Studio
  Vault Composer with real-time design
  AI suggestions from case data
  Story Thread integration
  Monument order flows through
  Family emotional connection
  Complete arrangement conference experience
  
Triguard products in Bridgeable:
  Basic order entry
  Standard catalog selection
  No personalization
  No Studio integration
  No AI suggestions
  No Story Thread
  
Which product does the funeral director
  present most enthusiastically?
Which product does the family
  connect with most deeply?
Which product generates more revenue?
Which product gets ordered more?

Wilbert wins on merit
Through the experience
Not through forced exclusion

Forced exclusivity creates resentment
Experience superiority creates loyalty
Experience superiority is permanent
Forced exclusivity is fragile
```

**The tiered supplier model:**

```
Wilbert — Premium Tier:
  Full Studio integration
  AI personalization
  Territory revenue on all digital products
  Preferred placement
  Complete arrangement conference experience
  Data intelligence partnership
  
Competing vault brands — Basic Tier:
  Standard order entry
  Basic catalog
  No Studio integration
  No AI personalization
  No territory revenue
  No data partnership
  
The platform is open
The tiers are differentiated
Wilbert's investment in the relationship
  shows up in the experience quality
  
A funeral home using Bridgeable
  sees Wilbert products presented
  with the full Studio treatment
  and competing products as
  standard order forms
  
That difference closes sales
Better than any exclusivity clause
More sustainably than any mandate
```

**The framing for the Wilbert CEO:**

```
"I heard the objection today
 about licensees who sell Triguard.
 I want to be transparent with you.
 
 Bridgeable manages the licensee's
 entire business — all their products.
 If they sell Triguard,
 they can order it through Bridgeable.
 
 Here's what actually happens though:
 
 Wilbert products go through
 the full Personalization Studio.
 Triguard products go through
 basic order entry.
 
 The funeral director who uses Bridgeable
 presents Wilbert products beautifully
 and Triguard products adequately.
 
 Families buy what gets presented well.
 
 Your market share grows not because
 licensees can't order Triguard —
 but because Wilbert products get
 an experience that Triguard never will.
 
 That's a better competitive position
 than forced exclusivity.
 Exclusivity creates resentment.
 Experience superiority creates loyalty."
```

**The mixed-product licensee at September:**

```
This licensee heard "tough luck" today
They will be at September

When you say:
  "Bridgeable manages your entire
   business — all your products"
   
Their hand goes up before
  you finish the sentence
  
They've been waiting for someone
  to say that all day
  
They become your most enthusiastic
  advocate in the room —
  representing the segment
  Wilbert just alienated
```

**The customer self-segmentation principle:**

A funeral home or licensee that chooses Wilbert's free ordering portal over Bridgeable was never going to transform their business. They wanted convenient ordering — that's all. They were never Bridgeable's customer with or without Wilbert's platform.

```
Wilbert's platform serves:
  "I want an easier way to order
   Wilbert products"
   → legitimate need
   → not Bridgeable's customer
   
Bridgeable serves:
  "I want to run a fundamentally
   different kind of business —
   one that generates $420,000 more
   revenue, serves families in a new way,
   and compounds in value every year"
   → Bridgeable's customer
   → was always Bridgeable's customer
   → Wilbert's platform doesn't touch them

These markets don't overlap
Wilbert's platform does not compete
  with Bridgeable for the same customer
  
Additionally — Wilbert's platform
  educates the market that technology
  belongs in death care
  validates the category
  makes Bridgeable adoption easier
  not harder
  
The funeral home that adopts
  Wilbert's basic portal
  and grows frustrated with its limits
  is a Bridgeable customer in waiting
```

### Wilbert Technology Stack — What Was Announced and What It Means

*Intelligence gathered April 13-14, 2026. All information from public announcements and licensee meeting.*

**The full stack:**

```
Epicor Kinetic:
  Internal manufacturing ERP
  Production, inventory, financials,
    shop floor management
  Already in use — being upgraded/redone
  The manufacturing backbone — appropriate
  Wilbert should own this layer
  
Epicor CPQ (Configure Price Quote):
  Visual product configurator
  Families/directors configure products visually
  Rules-based pricing
  Quote generation
  Manufacturing order output
  Embedded in the platform
  
OroCommerce:
  B2B ecommerce ordering platform
  External portal for licensees
    and funeral homes
  Product catalog management
  Order management
  B2B pricing tiers
  
Integration architecture:
  CPQ → OroCommerce → Kinetic
  Three separate systems
  Multiple custom integrations
  Hourly sync between OroCommerce
    and Kinetic (not real-time)
  
Licensing model:
  Free to licensees and funeral homes
  Wilbert absorbs all costs
  
Launch target: June 2027
  (with rebrand)
  Likely slips to Q3-Q4 2027 or 2028
  
Integration for licensees:
  API access provided
  Licensees told to figure out
    their own integrations
  Practical adoption ceiling: ~40%
    of licensees have no technical
    resources to self-integrate
```

**Critical technical weaknesses:**

```
1. Hourly OroCommerce → Kinetic sync:
   Not real-time
   Family approves vault at 10:47am
   Licensee doesn't see it until 11:47am
   In death care — hourly is the wrong
     answer to a grieving family's question
   "Has the order been placed?"
   
2. "Figure it out yourself" API:
   250 precast plant owners
   have no developers
   ~80% will never successfully
     integrate on their own
   Adoption ceiling: ~40% of network
   
3. No arrangement conference:
   Architecturally impossible with
     OroCommerce + CPQ
   These tools don't know who died
   They are product configurators
   Not arrangement conference platforms
   The moment that generates the sale
     is invisible to their entire stack
     
4. Three-system complexity:
   Kinetic + CPQ + OroCommerce
   Three vendors
   Three contracts
   Three integrations to maintain
   Three support relationships
   Three training programs
   Breaking changes when any system updates
   
5. June 2027 timeline:
   OroCommerce 250-licensee rollout: 12-18 months
   Epicor CPQ implementation: 6-12 months
   Kinetic upgrade: ongoing
   Rebrand: 3-6 months
   Real launch: likely 2028
   Bridgeable September 2026:
     9-18 months ahead minimum
```

**The Bridgeable architecture comparison:**

```
Wilbert stack:
  3 systems + integrations
  Hourly sync
  No arrangement conference
  No intelligence layer
  No case data
  40% practical adoption ceiling
  June 2027+ launch
  Complex vendor relationships
  
Bridgeable + Kinetic:
  2 systems (Bridgeable + Kinetic)
  Real-time webhook to Kinetic
  Full arrangement conference
  Full intelligence layer
  Complete case data
  100% practical adoption
    (no technical resources needed)
  September 2026 launch
  One clean integration
  Wilbert keeps manufacturing backbone
  Everything else handled by Bridgeable
```

**The offer — updated with full context:**

```
Cancel: OroCommerce
Cancel: Epicor CPQ
Keep:   Epicor Kinetic (manufacturing backbone)
Add:    Bridgeable → Kinetic real-time webhook
        (weeks of development, not months)

Wilbert gets:
  Everything OroCommerce provided ✓
  Everything CPQ provided ✓
  Plus arrangement conference ✓
  Plus intelligence layer ✓
  Plus family experience ✓
  Plus cross-tenant network ✓
  Plus GEICO data asset ✓
  Plus 100% licensee adoption
    (vs. 40% with self-serve API) ✓
  Plus September 2026
    (vs. June 2027+) ✓
  Plus $0 cost to Wilbert ✓

In exchange for:
  Endorsement at September meeting
  
The asymmetry of this deal
  is almost uncomfortable
  Wilbert gets everything
  Bridgeable gets endorsement
  Endorsement costs Wilbert nothing
  Everything Bridgeable provides
    is already built
```

## 6.12 Bridgeable Memorial Experiences — What Becomes Possible

Every personalized memorial product that exists today requires a family to find a vendor, commission the work, coordinate the timing, and manage the delivery — while they are grieving, in a 3-5 day window between death and service. The friction is humanly impossible at the worst possible time. So almost nobody does it.

Bridgeable removes every barrier simultaneously:

```
The case data IS the creative brief
The cross-tenant network IS the vendor connection
The intelligence layer IS the coordinator
The vault portal IS the approval mechanism
The family just says yes or no
```

This creates an entirely new category of memorial experience — products and moments that have never been standard because they were never logistically possible until now.

**The pattern that makes each one work:**

```
Scribe captures the person's life →
Intelligence layer identifies
  meaningful personalization →
Cross-tenant order placed with
  specialist vendor automatically →
Family approves through vault portal →
Product arrives at funeral home
  or service location →
Director presents it →
Family is moved →
They tell everyone →
Referral is permanent
```

---

### The Living Memorial Broadcast

During the service, a curated live feed of tributes, memories, and messages from people who couldn't attend — displayed on screens in real time as the service happens.

```
What exists today:
  Static slideshow of pre-selected photos
  Maybe a livestream for remote viewers

What Bridgeable makes possible:
  Family vault portal shared with
    extended network before service →
  Friends and family submit video tributes,
    written memories, photos in advance →
  Intelligence layer curates and sequences
    the most meaningful ones →
  During the service a live "memory wall"
    displays — tributes appearing as people
    watch, like a living portrait of impact

A man's Army buddy in Texas records a
  30-second video the morning of the service
It plays during the eulogy
His family sees it happen in real time

That has never been possible before
The coordination required was impossible
without a platform connecting everyone
```

**Why this generates referrals:** Every person in that room sees something they've never seen at a funeral. They will describe it to the next person they know who loses someone.

---

### The Personalized Soundscape

The entire audio environment of the service personalized to the person who died — not generic organ music but a curated sonic portrait of their life.

```
Scribe captured:
  They loved the Grateful Dead
  They coached Little League for 20 years
  They were married at Niagara Falls
  They went to Mass every Sunday

Intelligence layer builds the soundtrack:
  Opening: their actual wedding song
    sourced and cleared automatically
  During the viewing: songs that defined
    the decades of their life, sequenced
    chronologically
  During the eulogy: ambient versions —
    present but not distracting
  Recessional: something that captures
    who they were leaving the church

A family member walks in and hears
  their father's favorite song playing
  before they even sit down

They didn't have to ask
They didn't even know it was possible
The platform knew
```

**Implementation:** Spotify/Apple Music API for sourcing. Licensing handled through platform. Director controls playback from tablet. Intelligence layer sequences automatically based on service timeline in vault.

---

### The Personalized Memorial Candle

A custom-poured memorial candle where every element is personalized — color, scent, label — given to family members at the service.

```
Not a generic white candle with a label:

Color: their favorite color or
  colors meaningful to their life

Scent — a fragrance meaningful to them:
  Pine for the outdoorsman
  Lavender for the gardener
  Coffee for the person whose kitchen
    always smelled like a fresh pot
  Fresh cut grass for the groundskeeper
  Ocean for the sailor

Label: their photo, name, dates,
  a meaningful quote from the Scribe

What Bridgeable makes possible:
  Case data triggers candle personalization →
  Order placed with candle supplier
    cross-tenant before the service →
  Arrives at funeral home ready for distribution →
  Director places one at each seat

The scent especially is profound:
  Smell is the most memory-connected sense
  A family member lights that candle
    at home a year later
  The scent brings them back
  They think of the funeral home
    that made that possible
  That referral happens automatically
```

**Revenue:** $15-35 per candle. 50 attendees = $750-1,750 per service. High margin, zero friction sourcing.

---

### The Living Memorial — Personalized Plant or Seed

A living plant or seed packet personalized to the person, given at the service or graveside.

```
Scribe captures: "spent every weekend
  in her garden, especially loved
  growing tomatoes from seed"

Intelligence layer:
  Sources heirloom tomato seeds
  Packaged in personalized envelope
  Printed with her photo and name

Every attendee leaves with something living
  that connects them to her

The craftsman → seed packets for
  plants they grew together
The outdoorsman → native wildflower seeds
  from their favorite hiking region
The devoted Catholic →
  a small rosemary plant
  (symbol of remembrance in the tradition)

This is not possible today
The coordination in 3-5 days is impossible
Without Bridgeable connecting the case,
  the supplier, and the timing automatically
```

**The graveside version:** Tree saplings. "Plant this where you want them to grow." The cemetery vertical can track planting locations. The family can visit the tree through the cemetery plot map in their vault.

---

### The Time Capsule Service

A physical or digital time capsule created during or after the service that opens at a future date — an anniversary, a grandchild's graduation, a family milestone.

```
Physical version:
  A beautiful box given to the family
  Contains: letters from attendees
    written at the service,
    meaningful objects, photos,
    a message from the deceased
    (if pre-planned)
  Sealed with a date — "open in 10 years"
  The vault records what's inside

Digital version:
  Messages recorded by attendees
    at the service via QR code on the program
  Uploaded to family vault
  Scheduled for delivery on a future date

"On what would have been your grandmother's
 100th birthday — here are messages
 from everyone who loved her"
```

**Why this is strategically profound for Bridgeable:**

```
The family vault must stay active
  for the time capsule to deliver
  
A family that has a time capsule
  scheduled for 10 years from now
  has a reason to maintain their
  family vault portal for 10 years
  
The funeral home is remembered
  not just at the service
  but every time the family opens
  the vault and sees it waiting
  
The referral happens again
  when the capsule delivers
  10 years later
```

---

### The Crowdsourced Memory Book

A professionally designed hardcover book about the person's life — crowdsourced from everyone who knew them, structured by AI, printed and delivered after the service.

```
Not a guestbook. Not a photo album.
A genuine memorial book:

  Chapters sourced from:
    Family stories (submitted via vault portal)
    Photos from family and attendees
    Tributes from friends and colleagues
    Work memories and life milestones

  AI structures them into a narrative
  Professional layout generated automatically
  Printed and bound like a real book

  "A Life Well Lived:
   The Story of [Name] as Told by
   the People Who Knew Him Best"

What Bridgeable makes possible:
  Family vault portal shared before service →
  Attendees submit via QR code at service →
  Intelligence layer structures narrative →
  Family reviews and approves through vault →
  Printed and delivered 2 weeks after service →

A family receives a book 2 weeks after
  the grief fog lifts
  when they can actually receive it

That book becomes a family heirloom
The funeral home is remembered
  for creating it forever
```

**Revenue:** $75-200 per book depending on size and quality. Most families order multiple copies for family members. Print-on-demand vendor integration cross-tenant.

---

### The Personalized Memorial Portrait

A commissioned artwork of the deceased created from photos in the family vault — in a style meaningful to their life.

```
Not AI clip art — genuine commissioned artwork:
  Oil painting style for the formal patriarch

    and selects appropriate artist style →
  Artist commissioned cross-tenant →

  Family approves through vault portal →
  Final piece shipped to family →

This is a $200-500 product that currently
  requires the family to:
    Find an artist
    Commission the work
    Coordinate timing
    All while grieving

Zero families do it
Not because they don't want it
Because the friction is impossible
  at the worst time of their lives

Bridgeable makes it frictionless
The platform does the coordination
The family just approves
```

Revenue: $3-15 per program vs. $0.50 standard

  vs. $100 for standard programs

# Part 7 — Cemetery Vertical

## Cemetery Financial Recovery Platform

### Cemetery Vertical — Strategic Context and Financial Recovery Platform

**Why cemeteries are the most financially distressed tenant category:**

```
The fundamental structural problem:
  Core product is a one-time sale
    to a customer who never buys again
  Maintenance obligation is permanent
    and growing every year
  A cemetery founded in 1890 maintains
    130 years of graves on the revenue
    base of remaining unsold plots
  Many are running out of land and revenue
    simultaneously while costs increase
    
Specific pain points:

  Revenue declining:
    Cremation reduces plot demand
    Pre-need sales poorly marketed
    No ancillary revenue streams
    Endowment funds underfunded
    No digital presence
    
  Costs growing:
    Labor-intensive grounds maintenance
    Aging equipment replacement
    Veterans section compliance
    State endowment fund regulation
    Manual paper-based administration
    
  The trap:
    Can't afford to close
      (permanent obligation to families)
    Can't afford to stay open
      at current operating model
    Structurally insolvent with no exit
```

**Why Bridgeable is uniquely positioned to solve this:**

No other platform connects the cemetery to the funeral home arrangement conference, the manufacturer, the family vault, the compliance system, the financial infrastructure, and the workforce sharing network simultaneously. Each of those connections unlocks a revenue or cost solution the cemetery cannot access any other way.

**The Catholic Cemetery Conference is a milestone in the master doc vertical roadmap. Walking into that conference with documented case studies of financially distressed cemeteries that Bridgeable stabilized is not a software demo — it is a rescue mission. Rescued institutions become the most loyal customers that exist.**

---

### Revenue Stream 1 — Pre-Need Sales Engine (Cross-Tenant)

```
The biggest untapped revenue source
  most cemeteries ignore entirely:

Current reality:
  Families don't think about cemeteries
    until someone dies
  At-need purchase happens under grief
    and time pressure
  Families don't compare or plan
  They often spend less than they would
    with advance planning

Bridgeable cross-tenant connection:
  Cemetery connected to funeral homes
    in their geographic area →
  Every arrangement conference surfaces
    pre-need plot availability in real time →
  "While you're here, would you like
   to secure your own plot
   near your loved one?" →
  Interactive plot map shows availability →
  Family selects and purchases
    during arrangement conference →
  Payment through Bridgeable Pay →
  Plot reserved in vault immediately →

The grief context accelerates conversion:
  Families are thinking about mortality
    in a way they never otherwise do
  The plot map shows their loved one's
    location — proximity is compelling
  The arrangement conference is already
    a purchase decision context

A cemetery capturing 20% of at-need
  families as pre-need customers
  transforms their revenue model:
  
  100 at-need services/year × 20% = 20 pre-need
  20 pre-need × $3,500 average = $70,000
  Plus companion pre-need (spouse, parents):
    additional 15 × $3,500 = $52,500
  Annual new pre-need revenue: ~$122,500
  Compounding year over year
```

---

Pricing tiers:
  Basic: $200/year (2 seasonal visits + photos)
  Standard: $400/year (6 visits including holidays)
  Premium: $600/year (monthly + all holidays + plantings)

Intelligence layer automates everything:
  Scheduling from vault calendar
  Holiday triggers automatic
  Photo documentation to vault
  Billing through Bridgeable Pay
  Renewal reminders 30 days before

For the cemetery:
  Recurring predictable revenue
    from families who already trust them
  Essentially zero incremental cost —
    grounds crew is already there

Revenue potential — 5,000 active families:

  Growing annually as more families adopt

  Genealogy researchers

  Paper records in filing cabinets

Bridgeable vault for historical records:

    veteran status, nationality →

Revenue model:

    for researchers
  API access for Ancestry.com,
    23andMe, FindAGrave: licensing fee
  Family history report:
    "Your family's history at
     St. Mary's Cemetery 1887-present"
    AI-generated, vault-delivered: $75-150

A cemetery with 10,000 interments
  and 100 years of records
  has a data asset currently generating
  zero revenue

Annual revenue potential: $15,000-40,000
  depending on cemetery age and size
  Growing as digitization completes
```

### Revenue Stream 7 — Green Burial Premium Section

```
Green burial is the fastest-growing
  segment in death care:

  No embalming required
  Biodegradable casket or shroud only
  Natural grave marker or GPS coordinates
  Land managed to return to natural state
  Significantly lower cost to family
  Driven by environmental values
    and younger demographics

Most traditional cemeteries:
  Don't offer green burial
  Don't know how to certify
  Don't know how to market it
  Miss the fastest-growing segment entirely

Bridgeable makes it accessible:

  Green burial certification guidance
    through compliance hub →
  Designated green section on plot map →
  Families with matching values
    surfaced green options during
    arrangement conference →
  Green burial vendors connected cross-tenant:
    biodegradable caskets,
    natural shrouds, native plantings →
  Certification maintained automatically →

  Green burial often commands premium
    despite lower product cost
    because of values alignment
  Families pay for the experience
    and the environmental commitment
  $500-2,000 premium over standard

New revenue from a segment the cemetery
  couldn't serve before and that
  grows larger every year
```

### Revenue Stream 8 — Endowment Fund Optimization

```
Most cemeteries are legally required
  to maintain a perpetual care endowment —
  a percentage of every plot sale
  set aside for permanent maintenance

Current problems:
  Often underfunded (past non-compliance)
  Parked in low-yield local bank CDs
  Manual tracking in spreadsheets
  State compliance reporting burden
  Audit risk from poor documentation

Bridgeable financial infrastructure:

  Every plot sale automatically routes
    required percentage to endowment →
  Fund balance tracked in vault in real time →
  Investment managed through Bridgeable Bank:
    Better returns than local bank CDs
    Transparent performance reporting
    FDIC insured →
  State compliance report auto-generated:
    Same one-prompt audit capability
    as manufacturing compliance hub →

Benefits:
  Better investment returns:
    Even 1% improvement on $500,000 fund
    = $5,000/year additional income
  Compliance risk eliminated:
    Audit package always ready
    No scrambling when regulator calls
  Underfunded fund remediation plan:
    Bridgeable models catch-up contributions
    Creates compliance pathway
    Protects cemetery from regulatory action

For Bridgeable Bank:
  Endowment funds are stable,
    long-term deposits
  Aggregated across hundreds of cemeteries
    = significant deposit base
  Relationship creates banking trust
    for all other cemetery financial products
```

### Cost Reduction — Shared Services Network

```
Cemetery operations have the same
  workforce sharing opportunities
  as every other physical economy business:

Grounds crew seasonality:
  Spring through fall: full capacity needed
  Winter: significantly reduced workload
  Currently: layoffs or paid idle time

Bridgeable Workforce sharing:
  Winter cemetery crew →
    shared with contractors (site prep/cleanup)
    shared with manufacturers (grounds)
    shared with landscaping companies
  Workers maintain full income year-round
  Cemetery reduces winter payroll burden
  Workers keep benefits through Benefits Trust

Equipment sharing:
  Cemetery equipment (mowers, backhoes,
    excavators, utility vehicles)
  Often idle in winter months
  Shared with contractors and landscapers
    through Bridgeable Workforce platform
  Rental income generated from idle equipment

Shared maintenance technician:
  Cemetery equipment joins the regional
    shared maintenance pool
  Same model as manufacturer pool
  Cemetery gets professional maintenance
    at fraction of full-time cost
  Equipment lifespan extended

Annual cost reduction potential:
  Workforce sharing savings: $30,000-60,000
  Equipment sharing income: $10,000-20,000
  Shared maintenance: $15,000-25,000
  Total: $55,000-105,000/year reduction
```

# Part 8 — Future Roadmap

## 8.1 Bridgeable Communications — Native Communications Platform

**Current state:** RingCentral (VoIP) + Deepgram (transcription) + Twilio (SMS) + Resend (email)
**Native target:** Bridgeable Communications — owned SIP infrastructure, SMS, email

**The intermediate step (implement now, delivers 90% of the value):**
```
RingCentral calls → transcribed by Deepgram → 
  transcript written to vault as communication VaultItem
Emails (forwarded/BCC'd to Bridgeable) → parsed → VaultItem
SMS via Twilio → VaultItem
```

Every communication becomes a first-class VaultItem immediately, without owning the infrastructure.

**What a communication VaultItem looks like:**
```
item_type: "communication"
channel: "call" | "sms" | "email"
direction: "inbound" | "outbound"
participants: [linked CRM VaultItems]
transcript: full text
sentiment: scored
topics_mentioned: [extracted by intelligence layer]
vault_items_referenced: [auto-linked orders, cases, quotes, invoices mentioned]
action_items: [extracted]
outcome: logged
cross_tenant_visible: true/false
```

**What native communications unlocks:**

1. **Complete relationship context** — When anyone contacts a tenant, the intelligence layer surfaces their complete vault before the conversation begins. Every prior call, order, case, quote, complaint, payment. No CRM data entry required.

2. **Supercharged call overlay** — The call overlay already surfaces vault items as topics are mentioned. With every communication as a VaultItem, it also surfaces prior conversation threads. Rep picks up a call knowing the last three times this person called and why.

3. **Autonomous follow-up** — Intelligence layer monitors communication gaps:
   - Quote sent, no response in 5 days, no follow-up → drafts follow-up → rep approves
   - Contractor called, left voicemail, no callback in 4 hours → notifies rep with full context pre-loaded
   - Funeral home asked about pricing on a call, no quote generated in 48 hours → flags to sales team

4. **Cross-tenant communication history** — When a funeral home calls a manufacturer, both sides see the same communication VaultItem. The manufacturer rep knows the last three orders, open delivery issues, and payment status before the director explains anything.

5. **Communication intelligence at scale** — Across all tenants, the intelligence layer identifies: which call patterns convert to orders, which follow-up timing works, which objections precede quote rejection, which communication patterns correlate with churn. Improves platform-wide over time.

6. **Compliance and audit** — Every communication automatically archived. FTC audit, dispute resolution, employee review, and training all have complete records without manual logging.

7. **The funeral home relationship implication** — A family calls three years after a service. The director pulls the family vault. Every communication since the arrangement is there. The director knows their name, their loved one, what they asked last time. That experience is not possible with any other platform.

**The native infrastructure path:**
Owning SIP + email + SMS infrastructure is a later-stage investment. The intermediate step of writing all communications to the vault delivers the relationship intelligence immediately. When native infrastructure is built, it is a backend swap — the VaultItem model and intelligence layer don't change.

---

## 8.2 Integrate Now, Make Native Later

| Layer | Integrate Now | Make Native |
|---|---|---|
| Payments | Stripe | Bridgeable Pay (ILC/banking charter) |
| Documents/Signing | WeasyPrint + DocuSign | **Bridgeable Documents** (section 3.12) |
| Email/SMS | Resend + Twilio | Bridgeable Communications (section 7.2) |
| Location/Maps | Google Maps API | Bridgeable Location Services |
| AI/LLM | Anthropic API | **Bridgeable Intelligence** (section 3.10) — unified layer, already being built |
| Accounting | Already native for manufacturing | Extend to all verticals |
| Core Data/Storage | Cloudflare R2 | **Bridgeable Core** (section 3.6, name TBD) — being built now |
| Communications | RingCentral + Deepgram + Twilio | Bridgeable Communications — intermediate step: all comms as VaultItems now |
| **Quoting** | **Claude API + web scraping** | **Bridgeable QuotingEngine (section 3.11) — being built now** |

---

## 8.3 Build Prompt Standards

The following rules apply to all build prompts:

1. **Always output as a code block in chat** (one-click copy).

2. **Start with the correct context instruction** — the set of docs Sonnet must read depends on whether the prompt touches the UI:

   - **UI-touching prompts** (any feature with new or modified frontend components, pages, tokens, styles, animations, or interaction patterns):
     > "Read `CLAUDE.md`, `DESIGN_LANGUAGE.md`, and `UI_UX_ARC.md` fully before writing any code."
     - `DESIGN_LANGUAGE.md` — visual treatment (colors, tokens, shadows, spacing, motion, accessibility)
     - `UI_UX_ARC.md` — interaction patterns and platform primitives (command bar, saved views, triage, spaces, NL creation, briefings, Phase 7 polish components)

   - **Non-UI prompts** (backend logic, migrations, services, agents, scheduler jobs, API routes, tests — no new frontend output):
     > "Read `CLAUDE.md` fully before writing any code."
     Loading design docs into a backend-only prompt wastes context budget and risks misapplication of visual rules to non-visual problems.

3. **Always end with:** instructions to seed staging with relevant test data and run Playwright + Claude API end-to-end tests.
